In this short Q\\u0026A, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fsasha-pimentel\\u0022\\u003ESasha Pimentel\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E discusses her curatorial approach and her own creative work.\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Chr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Ciframe allow=\\u0022accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\\u0022 allowfullscreen=\\u0022\\u0022 frameborder=\\u00220\\u0022 height=\\u0022315\\u0022 src=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FcWcT_zthrzs\\u0022 width=\\u0022560\\u0022\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fiframe\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Chr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cem\\u003ERead a shortened transcript of the interview:\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EPoets.org: How did you approach curating Poem-a-Day?\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESasha Pimentel: Because Im from the Philippines;and because I live in this area called border in El Paso-Jurez thats really an external attempt to impose a boundary on a land and peoples in order to name one part of the same land as one country, and one part of the same land as another country; and because I teach in a bilingual MFA program in Spanish and English with students from across the Amricas; the poetry I know speaks to, and works from, many languages and many histories, even as a poem is unfolding in a single present. So I really wantedto bring in poets who carry inside them a sense of place, and a sense of being, thats larger than the ways we often name belonging.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EThat means transnational writers. Writers who refute the boundaries that are often named upon us through geography, or through gender. Multilingual writers. That meant, for me, seeing the Academy of American Poetsthe word Americanas the Amricas, and not this Estadounidensidad thats too often assumed into the word American. And that meant using this extraordinary opportunity to curate into the canon a way to be in awe of how much poets use language to imagine, and speak, an unthreatened belonging.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESo I thought about the narrative arc of the month, how it might start with writers who question and refute the bounds placed upon the body, and space. And how later weeks might rise in tension with poets who are speaking their own rhythms, and their own measures, against historical violences which by force have attempted to shrink and constrain us, but against which those poets speak anyway. And in so speaking, they uncover that freedom, and that expansiveness, thats \\u003Cem\\u003Epossibility\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E in language. Even when theyre speaking from places of painful utterance.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EPoets.orgs Tara Jayakar talks of \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatasha-trethewey\\u0022\\u003ENatasha Tretheway\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, who invokes \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjalal-al-din-rumi\\u0022\\u003ERumi\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E: the wound is the place where the light enters you. I was looking for poets who could speak like that, who speak light into a wound.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAnd I was wondering how each week might arc narratively too, and how the month could just kind of end buoyantly, and in many languages.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cbr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EPoets.org: If you could direct readers to one poem in our collection at Poets.org that you havent curated, what would it be and why?\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESP: I think \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fpatricia-smith\\u0022\\u003EPatricia Smith\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E is our living North Star in poetry.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm going to talk about one poet in terms of another first, but \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fphilip-levine\\u0022\\u003EPhillip Levine\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E has a poem on Poets.org titled \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fstory\\u0022\\u003EA Story\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, in which he says: Make no mistake, a family was here. You see \u002F the path worn into the linoleum where the wood \u002F gray and certainly pine, shows through. And in her poem, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fincendiary-art\\u0022\\u003EIncendiary Art\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, the poem Im recommending, Patricia Smith insists on that kind of guarding, that insistence against effacement: that insistence through language that a person, and people, have lived, and are living..\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EI think thats one of the most valuable things we can do as artists, to say, stop, hold on. This life that a person lives, or has lived, that matters. That matters, and we value it with language. In Incendiary Art, Smith writes a poem that speaks a larger and more intimate truth about community, and a citys peopleagainst how the violences in cities of color are often misnamed into that terrible, small word, riot. Its such an awful word, riot, and she uses the wonder of the poetic line to speak towards what \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmajor-jackson\\u0022\\u003EMajor Jackson\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E calls exaltation..\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESmith will move in one line from the words their bodies, to the word art, and shell end her lines, even though shes talking about pain, with a word as big and rife with possibility as the word air.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAnd she speaks about violence without extending it; she names it, but she doesnt extend it. To me, Patricia Smith always names that which is most important in a language thats always true, always complex, exploratory, and swollen with kinetic energy. In the last lines of that poem, she says: Our sons dont burn their cities as a rule, \u002F born, as they are, up to their necks in fuel.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cbr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EPoets.org: Who are you reading right now?\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESP: Part of me is like,\\u003Cem\\u003E the news\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E, um, all the time. But then Im like, wait a minute, bring it back to literature, Sasha.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EI spent the morning typing up the two versions of \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjames-baldwin\\u0022\\u003EJames Baldwin\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003Es A Letter to My Nephew, how it first appeared in \\u003Cem\\u003EThe Progressive\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E in1962, versus the 1963 version in \\u003Cem\\u003EThe Fire Next Time\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E as My Dungeon Shook: Letter to My Nephew on the One Hundredth Anniversary of the Emancipation. I do this a lot, transcribe a writers text, and I do it a lot with Baldwin because its a way to enter, and be inside, his sentences. To see how hes working through his clauses, and his commas, and his punctuation. I dont think I ever understood the power of a comma until I started studying Baldwin. How he can just distill a clarity, and weight, into a part of language with the right pauses.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm reading Art Spiegelmans book, \\u003Cem\\u003ECo-Mix: A Retrospective of Comics, Graphics, and Scraps\\u003C\u002Fem\\u003E, that goes over his career, his graphics, his comics. Something fascinating to me in it is that it has all these pictures of his proposed covers for the New Yorker, including the covers that were rejected, and that were accepted. To be able, in this way, to see how an institution inside a living culture resists, or runs, with an artist.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm supposed to be talking about what Im reading, but I watch a lot of television, and I was just watching this comedy special of Tig Notaro, and theres this moment where, after a double mastectomy, she takes off her shirt, and she does the rest of her set shirtless, and its amazing. Its beautiful, and amazing, and wonderful. It really makes us question what limitations in gender have been applied to our torsos that Tigs act now refutes and stuns. And that kind of pushing and questioning of a cultures values is what Im thinking of when I read Art Spiegelman.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm also almost always just in the works, old and new, of \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fcathy-park-hong\\u0022\\u003ECathy Park Hong\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatalie-diaz\\u0022\\u003ENatalie Diaz\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmichael-torres\\u0022\\u003EMichael Torres\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMartin-Espada\\u0022\\u003EMartn Espada\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FGregory-Pardlo\\u0022\\u003EGregory Pardlo\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FPaisley-Rekdal\\u0022\\u003EPaisley Rekdal\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMonica-Youn\\u0022\\u003EMonica Youn\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, and \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FTarfia-Faizullah\\u0022\\u003ETarfia Faizullah\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003Eand oh, the stories ofbecause Im trying to see how these masters, these writers, are going in and out of time, and are somehow collapsing and creating time, all at once, in their writing.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cbr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EPoets.org: What are you currently working on now in your writing, teaching, or publishing life?\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003ESP: I just finished an essay about birds and fish, and how we might measure pain scientifically, but also how we might pass on harm, without meaning it, one to another.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAnd Im working on a series of poems that are trying to reconcile the familial with the personal, and the postcolonial: what we name, and where we keep our silences. The poems take place in the US, the Philippines, Germany, and Latin America. I was really lucky to get to live, and teach, in Leipzig, Germany, at Universitt Leipzig. In Germany, the sense of monuments, and history, is so different than in the U.S. Their Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe, that agony and that history, is visible from the Reichstag, the German Parliament in Berlin. And we hear about this in the U.S. news, constantly, right now: which monuments we contest, and which monuments we stand by. So Ive been thinking about how we make monuments in space and language, culturally, and personally. And what that might mean when we rememberand when we refusememory.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm grateful to you all for the time to read and learn by guest editing Poem-a-Day. Ive learned so much from reading poems by these poets; I love their poems!\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIm also on a fellowship this semester, so Im really grateful to the National Endowment of the Arts, and my university, UTEP, for the time to read and write now. I feel like a kid, Im so excited for this rare time to get to read poetry, and to get to write it.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Chr \u002F\\u003E\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003E\\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-a-day\\u0022\\u003ERead Poem-a-Day\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E.\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003E\\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-day-guest-editors-2021\\u0022\\u003EBack to Guest Editors for 2021\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E.\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\",\n            \"image\": {\n                \"@type\": \"ImageObject\",\n                \"url\": \"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.poets.org\u002Fsites\u002Fdefault\u002Ffiles\u002Fcdsn9odz_400x400.png\",\n                \"width\": \"800\",\n                \"height\": \"800\"\n            },\n            \"datePublished\": \"Thu, 01\u002F28\u002F2021 - 18:07\",\n            \"dateModified\": \"Tue, 03\u002F02\u002F2021 - 14:28\",\n            \"author\": {\n                \"@type\": \"Organization\",\n                \"name\": \"Poets.org - Academy of American Poets\",\n                \"url\": \"https:\u002F\u002Fapi.poets.org\u002Fmarch-2021-poem-day-guest-editor-sasha-pimentel\",\n                \"logo\": {\n                    \"@type\": \"ImageObject\",\n                    \"url\": \"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.poets.org\u002Fsites\u002Fdefault\u002Ffiles\u002Flarge-blue-rgb-poets.org-logo-web.jpg\",\n                    \"width\": \"60\",\n                    \"height\": \"259\"\n                }\n            },\n            \"publisher\": {\n                \"@type\": \"Organization\",\n                \"name\": \"Poets.org - In this short Q&amp;A, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fsasha-pimentel\"\u003ESasha Pimentel\u003C\u002Fa\u003E discusses her curatorial approach and her own creative work.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FcWcT_zthrzs\" width=\"560\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ERead a shortened transcript of the interview:\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: How did you approach curating Poem-a-Day?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESasha Pimentel: Because Im from the Philippines;&nbsp;and because I live in this area called border in El Paso-Jurez thats really an external attempt to impose a boundary on a land and peoples in order to name one part of the same land as one country, and one part of the same land as another country; and because I teach in a bilingual MFA program in Spanish and English with students from across the Amricas; the poetry I know speaks to, and works from, many languages and many histories, even as a poem is unfolding in a single present. So I really wanted&nbsp;to bring in poets who carry inside them a sense of place, and a sense of being, thats larger than the ways we often name belonging.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EThat means transnational writers. Writers who refute the boundaries that are often named upon us through geography, or through gender. Multilingual writers. That meant, for me, seeing the Academy of American Poetsthe word Americanas the Amricas, and not this Estadounidensidad thats too often assumed into the word American. And that meant using this extraordinary opportunity to curate into the canon a way to be in awe of how much poets use language to imagine, and speak, an unthreatened belonging.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESo I thought about the narrative arc of the month, how it might start with writers who question and refute the bounds placed upon the body, and space. And how later weeks might rise in tension with poets who are speaking their own rhythms, and their own measures, against historical violences which by force have attempted to shrink and constrain us, but against which those poets speak anyway. And in so speaking, they uncover that freedom, and that expansiveness, thats \u003Cem\u003Epossibility\u003C\u002Fem\u003E in language. Even when theyre speaking from places of painful utterance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EPoets.orgs Tara Jayakar talks of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatasha-trethewey\"\u003ENatasha Tretheway\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, who invokes \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjalal-al-din-rumi\"\u003ERumi\u003C\u002Fa\u003E: the wound is the place where the light enters you. I was looking for poets who could speak like that, who speak light into a wound.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd I was wondering how each week might arc narratively too, and how the month could just kind of end buoyantly, and in many languages.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: If you could direct readers to one poem in our collection at Poets.org that you havent curated, what would it be and why?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: I think \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fpatricia-smith\"\u003EPatricia Smith\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is our living North Star in poetry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm going to talk about one poet in terms of another first, but \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fphilip-levine\"\u003EPhillip Levine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has a poem on Poets.org titled \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fstory\"\u003EA Story\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, in which he says: Make no mistake, a family was here. You see \u002F the path worn into the linoleum where the wood \u002F gray and certainly pine, shows through. And in her poem, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fincendiary-art\"\u003EIncendiary Art\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the poem Im recommending, Patricia Smith insists on that kind of guarding, that insistence against effacement: that insistence through language that a person, and people, have lived, and are living..\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EI think thats one of the most valuable things we can do as artists, to say, stop, hold on. This life that a person lives, or has lived, that matters. That matters, and we value it with language. In Incendiary Art, Smith writes a poem that speaks a larger and more intimate truth about community, and a citys peopleagainst how the violences in cities of color are often misnamed into that terrible, small word, riot. Its such an awful word, riot, and she uses the wonder of the poetic line to speak towards what \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmajor-jackson\"\u003EMajor Jackson\u003C\u002Fa\u003E calls exaltation..\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESmith will move in one line from the words their bodies, to the word art, and shell end her lines, even though shes talking about pain, with a word as big and rife with possibility as the word air.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd she speaks about violence without extending it; she names it, but she doesnt extend it. To me, Patricia Smith always names that which is most important in a language thats always true, always complex, exploratory, and swollen with kinetic energy. In the last lines of that poem, she says: Our sons dont burn their cities as a rule, \u002F born, as they are, up to their necks in fuel.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: Who are you reading right now?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: Part of me is like,\u003Cem\u003E the news\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, um, all the time. But then Im like, wait a minute, bring it back to literature, Sasha.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EI spent the morning typing up the two versions of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjames-baldwin\"\u003EJames Baldwin\u003C\u002Fa\u003Es A Letter to My Nephew, how it first appeared in \u003Cem\u003EThe Progressive\u003C\u002Fem\u003E in1962, versus the 1963 version in \u003Cem\u003EThe Fire Next Time\u003C\u002Fem\u003E as My Dungeon Shook: Letter to My Nephew on the One Hundredth Anniversary of the Emancipation. I do this a lot, transcribe a writers text, and I do it a lot with Baldwin because its a way to enter, and be inside, his sentences. To see how hes working through his clauses, and his commas, and his punctuation. I dont think I ever understood the power of a comma until I started studying Baldwin. How he can just distill a clarity, and weight, into a part of language with the right pauses.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm reading Art Spiegelmans book, \u003Cem\u003ECo-Mix: A Retrospective of Comics, Graphics, and Scraps\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, that goes over his career, his graphics, his comics. Something fascinating to me in it is that it has all these pictures of his proposed covers for the New Yorker, including the covers that were rejected, and that were accepted. To be able, in this way, to see how an institution inside a living culture resists, or runs, with an artist.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm supposed to be talking about what Im reading, but I watch a lot of television, and I was just watching this comedy special of Tig Notaro, and theres this moment where, after a double mastectomy, she takes off her shirt, and she does the rest of her set shirtless, and its amazing. Its beautiful, and amazing, and wonderful. It really makes us question what limitations in gender have been applied to our torsos that Tigs act now refutes and stuns. And that kind of pushing and questioning of a cultures values is what Im thinking of when I read Art Spiegelman.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also almost always just in the works, old and new, of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fcathy-park-hong\"\u003ECathy Park Hong\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatalie-diaz\"\u003ENatalie Diaz\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmichael-torres\"\u003EMichael Torres\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMartin-Espada\"\u003EMartn Espada\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FGregory-Pardlo\"\u003EGregory Pardlo\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FPaisley-Rekdal\"\u003EPaisley Rekdal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMonica-Youn\"\u003EMonica Youn\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FTarfia-Faizullah\"\u003ETarfia Faizullah\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eand oh, the stories ofbecause Im trying to see how these masters, these writers, are going in and out of time, and are somehow collapsing and creating time, all at once, in their writing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: What are you currently working on now in your writing, teaching, or publishing life?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: I just finished an essay about birds and fish, and how we might measure pain scientifically, but also how we might pass on harm, without meaning it, one to another.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd Im working on a series of poems that are trying to reconcile the familial with the personal, and the postcolonial: what we name, and where we keep our silences. The poems take place in the US, the Philippines, Germany, and Latin America. I was really lucky to get to live, and teach, in Leipzig, Germany, at Universitt Leipzig. In Germany, the sense of monuments, and history, is so different than in the U.S. Their Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe, that agony and that history, is visible from the Reichstag, the German Parliament in Berlin. And we hear about this in the U.S. news, constantly, right now: which monuments we contest, and which monuments we stand by. So Ive been thinking about how we make monuments in space and language, culturally, and personally. And what that might mean when we rememberand when we refusememory.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm grateful to you all for the time to read and learn by guest editing Poem-a-Day. Ive learned so much from reading poems by these poets; I love their poems!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also on a fellowship this semester, so Im really grateful to the National Endowment of the Arts, and my university, UTEP, for the time to read and write now. I feel like a kid, Im so excited for this rare time to get to read poetry, and to get to write it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-a-day\"\u003ERead Poem-a-Day\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-day-guest-editors-2021\"\u003EBack to Guest Editors for 2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n","format":"full_html","processed":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EIn 2021, the Academy of American Poets invited \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-day-guest-editors-2021\"\u003Etwelve poets\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to each curate a month of poems. How he can just distill a clarity, and weight, into a part of language with the right pauses.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm reading Art Spiegelmans book, \u003Cem\u003ECo-Mix: A Retrospective of Comics, Graphics, and Scraps\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, that goes over his career, his graphics, his comics. Something fascinating to me in it is that it has all these pictures of his proposed covers for the New Yorker, including the covers that were rejected, and that were accepted. To be able, in this way, to see how an institution inside a living culture resists, or runs, with an artist.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm supposed to be talking about what Im reading, but I watch a lot of television, and I was just watching this comedy special of Tig Notaro, and theres this moment where, after a double mastectomy, she takes off her shirt, and she does the rest of her set shirtless, and its amazing. Its beautiful, and amazing, and wonderful. It really makes us question what limitations in gender have been applied to our torsos that Tigs act now refutes and stuns. And that kind of pushing and questioning of a cultures values is what Im thinking of when I read Art Spiegelman.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also almost always just in the works, old and new, of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fcathy-park-hong\"\u003ECathy Park Hong\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatalie-diaz\"\u003ENatalie Diaz\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmichael-torres\"\u003EMichael Torres\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMartin-Espada\"\u003EMartn Espada\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FGregory-Pardlo\"\u003EGregory Pardlo\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FPaisley-Rekdal\"\u003EPaisley Rekdal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMonica-Youn\"\u003EMonica Youn\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FTarfia-Faizullah\"\u003ETarfia Faizullah\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eand oh, the stories ofbecause Im trying to see how these masters, these writers, are going in and out of time, and are somehow collapsing and creating time, all at once, in their writing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: What are you currently working on now in your writing, teaching, or publishing life?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: I just finished an essay about birds and fish, and how we might measure pain scientifically, but also how we might pass on harm, without meaning it, one to another.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd Im working on a series of poems that are trying to reconcile the familial with the personal, and the postcolonial: what we name, and where we keep our silences. The poems take place in the US, the Philippines, Germany, and Latin America. I was really lucky to get to live, and teach, in Leipzig, Germany, at Universitt Leipzig. In Germany, the sense of monuments, and history, is so different than in the U.S. Their Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe, that agony and that history, is visible from the Reichstag, the German Parliament in Berlin. And we hear about this in the U.S. news, constantly, right now: which monuments we contest, and which monuments we stand by. So Ive been thinking about how we make monuments in space and language, culturally, and personally. And what that might mean when we rememberand when we refusememory.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm grateful to you all for the time to read and learn by guest editing Poem-a-Day. Ive learned so much from reading poems by these poets; I love their poems!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also on a fellowship this semester, so Im really grateful to the National Endowment of the Arts, and my university, UTEP, for the time to read and write now. I feel like a kid, Im so excited for this rare time to get to read poetry, and to get to write it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca Black lives matter.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIn our mission to support poets, we must make unequivocally clear the essential and influential contributions that Black, Indigenous, and all poets of color have made and make to American poetry.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAs an organization devoted to poetry, we believe in the power of language to promote compassion and help us imagine new paths forward and a nation in which justice and equity are not just valued, but acted upon. We wanted to take this moment to remind cultural organizations of the importance of ensuring that people with disabilities are able to access these invaluable resources.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EBelow are some ways to create an inclusive experience for your virtual and digital events. Please let us know of other recommendations or needs from the field to better serve people with disabilities by emailing \\u003Ca href=\\u0022mailto:Accessibility@arts.gov\\u0022\\u003EAccessibility@arts.gov\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E. The National Endowment for the Arts does not endorse any vendors, but during this national emergency, the Office of Accessibility believes it is important to provide these resources to the arts community, including some examples of vendor options. You can find other vendors via internet search and recommendations from colleagues or from state or local disability agencies or organizations. Also, please note that this is a high-level overview and not a detailed how-to guide.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003ECommunication tip:\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E Be sure to include contact information on your website or event registration for requesting an access accommodation.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EStreamed and live-streamed performances\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWill the performance be live-captioned (preferred) or can the captions be included and synced up for later streaming?\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EReal-time captioning options:\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EVendor examples - \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\\u0022\\u003ENational Captioning Institute\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.captionaccess.com\u002F?fbclid=IwAR2k__5xDxbjaq-p7HH6wNaDa6fnupSrFwwm0iVng40Ss954nESMrfsHSOs\\u0022\\u003ECaptionAccess\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, and \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fstreamtext.net\u002F\\u0022\\u003EStreamtext\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EOther vendors are available via internet search.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EPost-production and DIY captioning options:\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EUpload video to YouTube and use the platform to add captions. Be sure to edit them because auto-generated captions are not always accurate.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EVendor examples - \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.rev.com\u002F\\u0022\\u003ERev.com\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.acscaptions.com\u002Fservices\u002Fpost-production-closed-captioning-service\u002F\\u0022\\u003EAlternative Communications Services\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, and \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.aslcaptions.com\u002F\\u0022\\u003EASLCaptions\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E. Other vendors are available via internet search.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EFor more information see \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Ftinachildress.wordpress.com\u002F2020\u002F03\u002F22\u002Fhow-to-caption-your-videos\u002F?fbclid=IwAR1KmX_KBSJZWoDxfQeb9sX20wsDluflU9Z3nNcR44mBAkOjauvnYLm3eYY\\u0022\\u003EHow to Caption Your Videos\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E - by Tina Childress, See Hear Communication Matters Blog.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWill you provide sign language interpretation in American Sign Language? (ASL) Many platforms allow sign language interpretation alongside the performance or discussion.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EASL interpreters can be found via the \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Frid.org\u002F\\u0022\\u003ERegistry of Interpreters for the Deaf\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, or search for ASL interpreting companies that offer video relay or video remote interpreting services.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EConsider adding visual description of your performance videos for people with vision disabilities. The \\u003Ca href=\\u0022http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002F\\u0022\\u003EAmerican Council of the Blind\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E has information on audio description, and a \\u003Ca href=\\u0022http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002Fservices.html\\u0022\\u003Elist of audio description vendors\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EVirtual exhibitions and collections\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWill all images include alternative text for people who are blind or have low vision and use screen-reading software? Alternative text (also called alt attribute, alt text, or alt-tag) is a visual description of an image that can be added using image formatting tools to describe the image for screen-reader users. Social media platforms also allow users to add alt text to their images before they are posted.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EEnsure videos are captioned and consider adding visual description (see above).\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EVideoconferencing \\u0026 webinars\\u003C\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWill the webinar be live-captioned? Note: Since webinars provide a platform for people to ask questions and interact with the speakers in real time, live captions allow people who are deaf or hard of hearing to participate in real time.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAre presenters making their material as accessible as possible? Be sure to:\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EDescribe all images used in the presentation.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EUse text that is high-contrast and in a large, legible font. Avoid italics and specialty or decorative fonts.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EBalance the need to provide visual information for visual learners with the need to keep the text concise.\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003C\u002Fli\\u003E\\n\\u003C\u002Ful\\u003E\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EReal-time captioning options:\\u003C\u002Fp\\u003E\\n\\u003Cul\\u003E\\u003Cli\\u003E\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EVendor examples - \\u003Ca href=\\u0022https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\\u0022\\u003ENational Captioning Institute\\u003C\u002Fa\\u003E, \\u003Ca We invite you to list your virtual events on our online \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoetry-near-you\"\u003EPoetry Near You calendar\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cstrong\u003EResources:&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.vidaweb.org\u002Fconformitys-labor-tips-to-make-poetry-events-more-accessible-to-people-who-are-d-deaf-or-hard-of-hearing\u002F\"\u003EConformitys Labor &amp; Tips to Make Poetry Events More Accessible to People Who Are D\u002FDeaf or Hard of Hearing\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&nbsp;by Camisha Jones\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.arts.gov\u002Faccessibility\u002Faccessibility-resources\u002Fnea-office-accessibility\"\u003ENational Endowment for the Arts&nbsp;Office of Accessibility\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n\u003Cstrong\u003EResources to Help Ensure Accessibility of Your Virtual Events for People with Disabilities\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EFrom the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.arts.gov\u002Faccessibility\u002Faccessibility-resources\u002Fnea-office-accessibility\"\u003ENational Endowment for the Arts&nbsp;Office of Accessibility\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\r\n&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EDear Arts and Culture Professionals,\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003ESince the start of the current Covid-19 crisis, artists and arts and culture organizations have been proactive in reaching out to their audiences and communities with webinars, livestreamed performances, and virtual visual art collections and museum tours. We wanted to take this moment to remind cultural organizations of the importance of ensuring that people with disabilities are able to access these invaluable resources.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003EBelow are some ways to create an inclusive experience for your virtual and digital events. Please let us know of other recommendations or needs from the field to better serve people with disabilities by emailing Accessibility@arts.gov. The National Endowment for the Arts does not endorse any vendors, but during this national emergency, the Office of Accessibility believes it is important to provide these resources to the arts community, including some examples of vendor options. You can find other vendors via internet search and recommendations from colleagues or from state or local disability agencies or organizations. Also, please note that this is a high-level overview and not a detailed how-to guide.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECommunication tip:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Be sure to include contact information on your website or event registration for requesting an access accommodation.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EStreamed and live-streamed performances\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EWill the performance be live-captioned (preferred) or can the captions be included and synced up for later streaming?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning options:&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\"\u003ENational Captioning Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.captionaccess.com\u002F?fbclid=IwAR2k__5xDxbjaq-p7HH6wNaDa6fnupSrFwwm0iVng40Ss954nESMrfsHSOs\"\u003ECaptionAccess\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstreamtext.net\u002F\"\u003EStreamtext\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cp\u003EOther vendors are available via internet search.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EPost-production and DIY captioning options:&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cp\u003EUpload video to YouTube and use the platform to add captions. Be sure to edit them because auto-generated captions are not always accurate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.rev.com\u002F\"\u003ERev.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.acscaptions.com\u002Fservices\u002Fpost-production-closed-captioning-service\u002F\"\u003EAlternative Communications Services\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.aslcaptions.com\u002F\"\u003EASLCaptions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Other vendors are available via internet search.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003Cp\u003EFor more information see \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftinachildress.wordpress.com\u002F2020\u002F03\u002F22\u002Fhow-to-caption-your-videos\u002F?fbclid=IwAR1KmX_KBSJZWoDxfQeb9sX20wsDluflU9Z3nNcR44mBAkOjauvnYLm3eYY\"\u003EHow to Caption Your Videos\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - by Tina Childress, See Hear Communication Matters Blog.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EWill you provide sign language interpretation in American Sign Language? (ASL) Many platforms allow sign language interpretation alongside the performance or discussion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EASL interpreters can be found via the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Frid.org\u002F\"\u003ERegistry of Interpreters for the Deaf\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, or search for ASL interpreting companies that offer video relay or video remote interpreting services.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EConsider adding visual description of your performance videos for people with vision disabilities. The \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002F\"\u003EAmerican Council of the Blind\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has information on audio description, and a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002Fservices.html\"\u003Elist of audio description vendors\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVirtual exhibitions and collections\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EWill all images include alternative text for people who are blind or have low vision and use screen-reading software? Alternative text (also called alt attribute, alt text, or alt-tag) is a visual description of an image that can be added using image formatting tools to describe the image for screen-reader users. Social media platforms also allow users to add alt text to their images before they are posted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EEnsure videos are captioned and consider adding visual description (see above).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVideoconferencing &amp; webinars\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EWill the webinar be live-captioned? Note: Since webinars provide a platform for people to ask questions and interact with the speakers in real time, live captions allow people who are deaf or hard of hearing to participate in real time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EAre presenters making their material as accessible as possible? Be sure to:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EDescribe all images used in the presentation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EUse text that is high-contrast and in a large, legible font. Avoid italics and specialty or decorative fonts.&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EBalance the need to provide visual information for visual learners with the need to keep the text concise.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\t\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\r\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning options:&nbsp;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\r\n\r\n\t\u003Cul\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cli\u003E\r\n\t\t\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\"\u003ENational We will be updating this list in the days and weeks ahead. We invite you to list your virtual events on our online \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoetry-near-you\"\u003EPoetry Near You calendar\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EResources:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.vidaweb.org\u002Fconformitys-labor-tips-to-make-poetry-events-more-accessible-to-people-who-are-d-deaf-or-hard-of-hearing\u002F\"\u003EConformitys Labor &amp; Tips to Make Poetry Events More Accessible to People Who Are D\u002FDeaf or Hard of Hearing\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eby Camisha Jones\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.arts.gov\u002Faccessibility\u002Faccessibility-resources\u002Fnea-office-accessibility\"\u003ENational Endowment for the ArtsOffice of Accessibility\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EResources to Help Ensure Accessibility of Your Virtual Events for People with Disabilities\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFrom the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.arts.gov\u002Faccessibility\u002Faccessibility-resources\u002Fnea-office-accessibility\"\u003ENational Endowment for the ArtsOffice of Accessibility\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDear Arts and Culture Professionals,\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESince the start of the current Covid-19 crisis, artists and arts and culture organizations have been proactive in reaching out to their audiences and communities with webinars, livestreamed performances, and virtual visual art collections and museum tours. We wanted to take this moment to remind cultural organizations of the importance of ensuring that people with disabilities are able to access these invaluable resources.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBelow are some ways to create an inclusive experience for your virtual and digital events. Please let us know of other recommendations or needs from the field to better serve people with disabilities by emailing \u003Ca href=\"mailto:Accessibility@arts.gov\"\u003EAccessibility@arts.gov\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The National Endowment for the Arts does not endorse any vendors, but during this national emergency, the Office of Accessibility believes it is important to provide these resources to the arts community, including some examples of vendor options. You can find other vendors via internet search and recommendations from colleagues or from state or local disability agencies or organizations. Also, please note that this is a high-level overview and not a detailed how-to guide.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECommunication tip:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Be sure to include contact information on your website or event registration for requesting an access accommodation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EStreamed and live-streamed performances\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill the performance be live-captioned (preferred) or can the captions be included and synced up for later streaming?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning options:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\"\u003ENational Captioning Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.captionaccess.com\u002F?fbclid=IwAR2k__5xDxbjaq-p7HH6wNaDa6fnupSrFwwm0iVng40Ss954nESMrfsHSOs\"\u003ECaptionAccess\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstreamtext.net\u002F\"\u003EStreamtext\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOther vendors are available via internet search.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPost-production and DIY captioning options:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUpload video to YouTube and use the platform to add captions. Be sure to edit them because auto-generated captions are not always accurate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.rev.com\u002F\"\u003ERev.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.acscaptions.com\u002Fservices\u002Fpost-production-closed-captioning-service\u002F\"\u003EAlternative Communications Services\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.aslcaptions.com\u002F\"\u003EASLCaptions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Other vendors are available via internet search.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor more information see \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftinachildress.wordpress.com\u002F2020\u002F03\u002F22\u002Fhow-to-caption-your-videos\u002F?fbclid=IwAR1KmX_KBSJZWoDxfQeb9sX20wsDluflU9Z3nNcR44mBAkOjauvnYLm3eYY\"\u003EHow to Caption Your Videos\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - by Tina Childress, See Hear Communication Matters Blog.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill you provide sign language interpretation in American Sign Language? (ASL) Many platforms allow sign language interpretation alongside the performance or discussion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EASL interpreters can be found via the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Frid.org\u002F\"\u003ERegistry of Interpreters for the Deaf\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, or search for ASL interpreting companies that offer video relay or video remote interpreting services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EConsider adding visual description of your performance videos for people with vision disabilities. The \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002F\"\u003EAmerican Council of the Blind\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has information on audio description, and a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002Fservices.html\"\u003Elist of audio description vendors\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVirtual exhibitions and collections\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill all images include alternative text for people who are blind or have low vision and use screen-reading software? Alternative text (also called alt attribute, alt text, or alt-tag) is a visual description of an image that can be added using image formatting tools to describe the image for screen-reader users. Social media platforms also allow users to add alt text to their images before they are posted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEnsure videos are captioned and consider adding visual description (see above).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVideoconferencing &amp; webinars\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill the webinar be live-captioned? Note: Since webinars provide a platform for people to ask questions and interact with the speakers in real time, live captions allow people who are deaf or hard of hearing to participate in real time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAre presenters making their material as accessible as possible? Be sure to:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDescribe all images used in the presentation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUse text that is high-contrast and in a large, legible font. Avoid italics and specialty or decorative fonts.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBalance the need to provide visual information for visual learners with the need to keep the text concise.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning attend free\" data-entity-type=\"file\" data-entity-uuid=\"00736c27-e702-4710-8b10-4618d1519a5a\" height=\"35\" src=\"\u002Fsites\u002Fdefault\u002Ffiles\u002Finline-images\u002FButtons2.png\" width=\"193\" \u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\nPoetry &amp; the Creative Mind features leading and legendary actors, dancers, artists, musicians, and public figures sharing their favorite poems. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fgala\u002Fpast-readers\"\u003EPast readers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E have included Uzo Aduba, Sam Beam, Wayne Brady, Glenn Close, Claire Danes, Tina Fey, Terrance Howard, Bill T. Jones, Maya Lin, Paul Simon, Patti Smith, Uma Thurman, and Carrie Mae Weems, as well as frequent Honorary Event Co-chair Meryl Streep.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EThis always-inspiring evening benefits the K12 Education Program of the Academy of American Poets, which reaches more than 100,000 students each year with resources on Poets.org, the Dear Poet project, and materials created for \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fnode\u002F11257\"\u003ENational Poetry Month\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Academy of American Poets had hosted this annual celebration each year from 20032019. In 2020, due to the coronavirus pandemic, the event, which gathers a thousand poetry readers together at Lincoln Centers Alice Tully Hall, could not be held as planned. A virtual reading called Shelter in Poems was held in its place, as an opportunity to find community together in poetry during an unprecedented moment in history. \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fshelter-poems\"\u003ERevisit that event recording and read poems from the Shelter in Poems collection here\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EPoetry &amp; the Creative Mind is made possible thanks to the support of individuals and the events corporate sponsors. This year, in honor of the 25th anniversary of National Poetry Monthnow the largest literary celebration in the worldthe Academy of American Poets will recognize the publishers and companies helping to champion poetry and expand its readership, including to young audiences across the country, as part of The Publishers Circle and The Young Readers Circle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ETo learn about this years special opportunities for corporate sponsorship of Poetry &amp; the Creative Mind on April 29, 2021 and the 25th annual celebration of National Poetry Month\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"mailto:mcampagna@poets.org\"\u003Eemail michelle campagna, marketing &amp; advertising senior manager &gt;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n","link":"\u002Facademy-american-poets\u002Fprograms\u002Fpoetry-creative-mind","img":{"src":"https:\u002F\u002Fapi.poets.org\u002Fsites\u002Fdefault\u002Ffiles\u002Fstyles\u002Ffeature\u002Fpublic\u002F2021-02\u002FPCM_FeatureBlock_2021.png?itok=lybGIAvn","alt":"Poetry & the Creative Mind","title":"Poetry & the Creative Mind"}},{"title":"March 2021 Poem-a-Day Guest Editor Sasha Pimentel","subtitle":"Interview ","text":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EIn 2021, the Academy of American Poets invited \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-day-guest-editors-2021\"\u003Etwelve poets\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to each curate a month of poems. In this short Q&amp;A, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fsasha-pimentel\"\u003ESasha Pimentel\u003C\u002Fa\u003E discusses her curatorial approach and her own creative work.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"315\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FcWcT_zthrzs\" width=\"560\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ERead a shortened transcript of the interview:\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: How did you approach curating Poem-a-Day?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESasha Pimentel: Because Im from the Philippines;and because I live in this area called border in El Paso-Jurez thats really an external attempt to impose a boundary on a land and peoples in order to name one part of the same land as one country, and one part of the same land as another country; and because I teach in a bilingual MFA program in Spanish and English with students from across the Amricas; the poetry I know speaks to, and works from, many languages and many histories, even as a poem is unfolding in a single present. So I really wantedto bring in poets who carry inside them a sense of place, and a sense of being, thats larger than the ways we often name belonging.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EThat means transnational writers. Writers who refute the boundaries that are often named upon us through geography, or through gender. Multilingual writers. That meant, for me, seeing the Academy of American Poetsthe word Americanas the Amricas, and not this Estadounidensidad thats too often assumed into the word American. And that meant using this extraordinary opportunity to curate into the canon a way to be in awe of how much poets use language to imagine, and speak, an unthreatened belonging.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESo I thought about the narrative arc of the month, how it might start with writers who question and refute the bounds placed upon the body, and space. And how later weeks might rise in tension with poets who are speaking their own rhythms, and their own measures, against historical violences which by force have attempted to shrink and constrain us, but against which those poets speak anyway. And in so speaking, they uncover that freedom, and that expansiveness, thats \u003Cem\u003Epossibility\u003C\u002Fem\u003E in language. Even when theyre speaking from places of painful utterance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EPoets.orgs Tara Jayakar talks of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatasha-trethewey\"\u003ENatasha Tretheway\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, who invokes \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjalal-al-din-rumi\"\u003ERumi\u003C\u002Fa\u003E: the wound is the place where the light enters you. I was looking for poets who could speak like that, who speak light into a wound.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd I was wondering how each week might arc narratively too, and how the month could just kind of end buoyantly, and in many languages.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: If you could direct readers to one poem in our collection at Poets.org that you havent curated, what would it be and why?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: I think \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fpatricia-smith\"\u003EPatricia Smith\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is our living North Star in poetry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm going to talk about one poet in terms of another first, but \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fphilip-levine\"\u003EPhillip Levine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has a poem on Poets.org titled \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fstory\"\u003EA Story\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, in which he says: Make no mistake, a family was here. You see \u002F the path worn into the linoleum where the wood \u002F gray and certainly pine, shows through. And in her poem, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem\u002Fincendiary-art\"\u003EIncendiary Art\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the poem Im recommending, Patricia Smith insists on that kind of guarding, that insistence against effacement: that insistence through language that a person, and people, have lived, and are living..\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EI think thats one of the most valuable things we can do as artists, to say, stop, hold on. This life that a person lives, or has lived, that matters. That matters, and we value it with language. In Incendiary Art, Smith writes a poem that speaks a larger and more intimate truth about community, and a citys peopleagainst how the violences in cities of color are often misnamed into that terrible, small word, riot. Its such an awful word, riot, and she uses the wonder of the poetic line to speak towards what \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmajor-jackson\"\u003EMajor Jackson\u003C\u002Fa\u003E calls exaltation..\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESmith will move in one line from the words their bodies, to the word art, and shell end her lines, even though shes talking about pain, with a word as big and rife with possibility as the word air.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd she speaks about violence without extending it; she names it, but she doesnt extend it. To me, Patricia Smith always names that which is most important in a language thats always true, always complex, exploratory, and swollen with kinetic energy. In the last lines of that poem, she says: Our sons dont burn their cities as a rule, \u002F born, as they are, up to their necks in fuel.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: Who are you reading right now?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: Part of me is like,\u003Cem\u003E the news\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, um, all the time. But then Im like, wait a minute, bring it back to literature, Sasha.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EI spent the morning typing up the two versions of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fjames-baldwin\"\u003EJames Baldwin\u003C\u002Fa\u003Es A Letter to My Nephew, how it first appeared in \u003Cem\u003EThe Progressive\u003C\u002Fem\u003E in1962, versus the 1963 version in \u003Cem\u003EThe Fire Next Time\u003C\u002Fem\u003E as My Dungeon Shook: Letter to My Nephew on the One Hundredth Anniversary of the Emancipation. I do this a lot, transcribe a writers text, and I do it a lot with Baldwin because its a way to enter, and be inside, his sentences. To see how hes working through his clauses, and his commas, and his punctuation. I dont think I ever understood the power of a comma until I started studying Baldwin. How he can just distill a clarity, and weight, into a part of language with the right pauses.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm reading Art Spiegelmans book, \u003Cem\u003ECo-Mix: A Retrospective of Comics, Graphics, and Scraps\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, that goes over his career, his graphics, his comics. Something fascinating to me in it is that it has all these pictures of his proposed covers for the New Yorker, including the covers that were rejected, and that were accepted. To be able, in this way, to see how an institution inside a living culture resists, or runs, with an artist.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm supposed to be talking about what Im reading, but I watch a lot of television, and I was just watching this comedy special of Tig Notaro, and theres this moment where, after a double mastectomy, she takes off her shirt, and she does the rest of her set shirtless, and its amazing. Its beautiful, and amazing, and wonderful. It really makes us question what limitations in gender have been applied to our torsos that Tigs act now refutes and stuns. And that kind of pushing and questioning of a cultures values is what Im thinking of when I read Art Spiegelman.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also almost always just in the works, old and new, of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fcathy-park-hong\"\u003ECathy Park Hong\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fnatalie-diaz\"\u003ENatalie Diaz\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002Fmichael-torres\"\u003EMichael Torres\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMartin-Espada\"\u003EMartn Espada\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FGregory-Pardlo\"\u003EGregory Pardlo\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FPaisley-Rekdal\"\u003EPaisley Rekdal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FMonica-Youn\"\u003EMonica Youn\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoet\u002FTarfia-Faizullah\"\u003ETarfia Faizullah\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eand oh, the stories ofbecause Im trying to see how these masters, these writers, are going in and out of time, and are somehow collapsing and creating time, all at once, in their writing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr \u002F\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPoets.org: What are you currently working on now in your writing, teaching, or publishing life?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003ESP: I just finished an essay about birds and fish, and how we might measure pain scientifically, but also how we might pass on harm, without meaning it, one to another.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd Im working on a series of poems that are trying to reconcile the familial with the personal, and the postcolonial: what we name, and where we keep our silences. The poems take place in the US, the Philippines, Germany, and Latin America. I was really lucky to get to live, and teach, in Leipzig, Germany, at Universitt Leipzig. In Germany, the sense of monuments, and history, is so different than in the U.S. Their Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe, that agony and that history, is visible from the Reichstag, the German Parliament in Berlin. And we hear about this in the U.S. news, constantly, right now: which monuments we contest, and which monuments we stand by. So Ive been thinking about how we make monuments in space and language, culturally, and personally. And what that might mean when we rememberand when we refusememory.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm grateful to you all for the time to read and learn by guest editing Poem-a-Day. Ive learned so much from reading poems by these poets; I love their poems!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003EIm also on a fellowship this semester, so Im really grateful to the National Endowment of the Arts, and my university, UTEP, for the time to read and write now. I feel like a kid, Im so excited for this rare time to get to read poetry, and to get to write it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Chr \u002F\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-a-day\"\u003ERead Poem-a-Day\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fpoem-day-guest-editors-2021\"\u003EBack to Guest Editors for 2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n","link":"\u002Fmarch-2021-poem-day-guest-editor-sasha-pimentel","img":{"src":"https:\u002F\u002Fapi.poets.org\u002Fsites\u002Fdefault\u002Ffiles\u002Fstyles\u002Ffeature\u002Fpublic\u002F2021-03\u002FSasha%20Pimentel_homepage%20696x486_Credit%20Jorge%20Salgado.png?itok=A41LnVtl","alt":"Sasha Pimentel_homepage 696x486_Credit Jorge Salgado","title":"Sasha Pimentel_homepage 696x486_Credit Jorge Salgado"}},{"title":"COVID-19 Resources for Poets, Writers, and Poetry Organizations","subtitle":"Resource ","text":"\u003Cp\u003ETo support poets, writers, and artists during the COVID-19 crisis, the Academy of American Points has joined a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpoets.org\u002Fcoalition-arts-funders-launches-emergency-artist-relief-fund\"\u003Ecoalition of national arts grantmakers\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eto create an emergency initiative to offer financial and informational resources to artists across the United States. \u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.artistrelief.org\"\u003EArtist Relief\u003C\u002Fa\u003Ewill distribute $5,000 grants to artists facing dire financial emergencies due to COVID-19\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E; We wanted to take this moment to remind cultural organizations of the importance of ensuring that people with disabilities are able to access these invaluable resources.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBelow are some ways to create an inclusive experience for your virtual and digital events. Please let us know of other recommendations or needs from the field to better serve people with disabilities by emailing \u003Ca href=\"mailto:Accessibility@arts.gov\"\u003EAccessibility@arts.gov\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The National Endowment for the Arts does not endorse any vendors, but during this national emergency, the Office of Accessibility believes it is important to provide these resources to the arts community, including some examples of vendor options. You can find other vendors via internet search and recommendations from colleagues or from state or local disability agencies or organizations. Also, please note that this is a high-level overview and not a detailed how-to guide.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECommunication tip:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Be sure to include contact information on your website or event registration for requesting an access accommodation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EStreamed and live-streamed performances\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill the performance be live-captioned (preferred) or can the captions be included and synced up for later streaming?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning options:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\"\u003ENational Captioning Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.captionaccess.com\u002F?fbclid=IwAR2k__5xDxbjaq-p7HH6wNaDa6fnupSrFwwm0iVng40Ss954nESMrfsHSOs\"\u003ECaptionAccess\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstreamtext.net\u002F\"\u003EStreamtext\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOther vendors are available via internet search.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPost-production and DIY captioning options:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUpload video to YouTube and use the platform to add captions. Be sure to edit them because auto-generated captions are not always accurate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.rev.com\u002F\"\u003ERev.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.acscaptions.com\u002Fservices\u002Fpost-production-closed-captioning-service\u002F\"\u003EAlternative Communications Services\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.aslcaptions.com\u002F\"\u003EASLCaptions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Other vendors are available via internet search.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor more information see \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftinachildress.wordpress.com\u002F2020\u002F03\u002F22\u002Fhow-to-caption-your-videos\u002F?fbclid=IwAR1KmX_KBSJZWoDxfQeb9sX20wsDluflU9Z3nNcR44mBAkOjauvnYLm3eYY\"\u003EHow to Caption Your Videos\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - by Tina Childress, See Hear Communication Matters Blog.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill you provide sign language interpretation in American Sign Language? (ASL) Many platforms allow sign language interpretation alongside the performance or discussion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EASL interpreters can be found via the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Frid.org\u002F\"\u003ERegistry of Interpreters for the Deaf\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, or search for ASL interpreting companies that offer video relay or video remote interpreting services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EConsider adding visual description of your performance videos for people with vision disabilities. The \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002F\"\u003EAmerican Council of the Blind\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has information on audio description, and a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.acb.org\u002Fadp\u002Fservices.html\"\u003Elist of audio description vendors\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVirtual exhibitions and collections\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill all images include alternative text for people who are blind or have low vision and use screen-reading software? Alternative text (also called alt attribute, alt text, or alt-tag) is a visual description of an image that can be added using image formatting tools to describe the image for screen-reader users. Social media platforms also allow users to add alt text to their images before they are posted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEnsure videos are captioned and consider adding visual description (see above).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVideoconferencing &amp; webinars\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWill the webinar be live-captioned? Note: Since webinars provide a platform for people to ask questions and interact with the speakers in real time, live captions allow people who are deaf or hard of hearing to participate in real time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAre presenters making their material as accessible as possible? Be sure to:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDescribe all images used in the presentation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUse text that is high-contrast and in a large, legible font. Avoid italics and specialty or decorative fonts.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBalance the need to provide visual information for visual learners with the need to keep the text concise.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReal-time captioning options:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVendor examples - \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncicap.org\u002F\"\u003ENational Captioning Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.captionaccess.com\u002F?fbclid=IwAR2k__5xDxbjaq-p7HH6wNaDa6fnupSrFwwm0iVng40Ss954nESMrfsHSOs\"\u003ECaptionAccess\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca
